The expert interview analysis indicates a high focus on operational determinants related to the 
group Cost & Capital, where Net Working Capital is mentioned by all interviewed experts. The 
reasoning behind this immense focus is the importance of understanding the operational cost 
breakdown from an investor perspective. Hence, insights within this group provides crucial leverages 
==PAGE:74==
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
74 
 
74 
on where to focus the ODD efforts. Furthermore, this knowledge supports the acquirer's future wish 
to improve the cost structure and free up capital. In addition, the determinant group Planning, 
Efficiency & Quality is generally a profound focus area, as multiple expert stress these underlying 
determinants as drivers for significant operational improvement. The group with lowest focus is 
Politics & Regulations. However, the determinant Approvals & Certifications was mentioned by a 
several experts as a vital element of investigation as it pose a potential deal breaker. Yet, it is 
simultaneously highlighted as infrequent and very case specific.  
Another ascertainment concerns the general approach to operational due diligence. The majority 
of expert interviewees contemplate the ODD process from 1) a risk perspective, and 2) an 
improvement potential perspective. Both perspectives help provide key insights as leverage in the 
acquisition negotiation, to quantify the return of investment, help mitigate uncertainty, and avoid 
unexpected problems or costs/investments. 
Multiple experts accentuate the importance of understanding the target company's ability to scale 
and the maturity of the operating model. These two drivers, scalability and maturity, are not 
characterized as individual determinants as they stretch across multiple groups, e.g. the ability to scale 
the organizational structure and the production capacity, or the degree of maturity in IT systems and 
operational planning. Lastly, synergies and consolidation are mentioned in some interviews as a 
potential to cut cost and streamline the operating model. However, these elements are not considered 
as single determinants as they have highly influenced by interlinkages.  
Finally, an observation in the broader perspective of the operational due diligence is that all experts 
define the organizational scope as the supply chain. 
 
Comparative Analysis 
In general, there is a strong correlation between the extant literature and the expert interviews. Even 
though, the extant literature handles the operational due diligence subject in a less detailed degree 
than the experts. Due to the nature of the extant literature, the findings from the expert interviews 
embrace and cover the determinants identified in the literature review. Furthermore, the expert 
interviews presented several additional operational determinants, which further strengthen the 
exhaustiveness and depth of research on operational due diligence.  
 
The extant literature presented a narrowed focused perspective on scalability (Morrison, 2008; 
Emerald group, 2004; Shaughnessy, 2009), whereas the experts view this driver across the entire 
operating model of the target company. However, Tompkins (2012) share the expert’s holistic 
approach on scalability.   
One aspect which was highlighted by the experts was maturity as a measure across several of the 
operational determinants. This aspect of the operational due diligence is essentially a way to assess 
the current state of the target company and hereby helps address the overall impression of the 
operating model. Documentation and data quality is underlined by several experts as being closely 
interlinked with the target company’s overall maturity, while the subject of documentation and data 
related to operational activities is almost non-existing in the literature. 
 
The importance of understanding the target company's organization and the people involved in 
operational activities are widely and equivalently covered by both the extant literature and the 
interviewed experts. One difference is identified in the way of understanding the people’s 
competencies. While the extant literature considers the organization as unity, the experts present clear 
distinction between the executive and board leadership competencies and the workforce 
competencies. The further reasoning for the distinction is associated with the acquires immense focus 
on strategic understanding and ability to execute from a leadership perspective. 
==PAGE:75==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
75 
 
Referring to the previously mentioned depth of literature, the cost and capital aspect of the 
operational due diligence illustrate this part very well. While the literature presents cost and capital 
as a high level area of investigation, the experts break it down on a level of detail which can be related 
to the profit and loss statement and the balance sheet. Besides the degree of detail, the acquirer's insist 
on a direct and strong coupling between operational findings and the financial impact. 
 
The largest gap between the extant literature and the interview findings are also some of the most 
fundamental elements in the operating model from operations management perspective (Russel & 
Taylor, 2017). Even though, an extensive amount of extant literature helps describe a company’s 
operating model, it has yet to be structured and set in relation to the operational due diligence. Hence, 
this research seeks to address the previously defined aim by incorporate these elements in the 
operational due diligence. 
 
Conceptual Operation Due Diligence framework  
To accommodate the rising need for identification of operational determinants in a target company, 
both the literature review and empirical data recommended to utilize a structured and comprehensive 
approach to perform operational due diligence in mergers and acquisitions. Due to the time pressure 
in the process of an operational due diligence, the approach must be driven by determination and have 
multiple iterations – ensuring an efficient yet sufficient assessment. Therefore, a hypothesis driven 
framework is optimal, which incorporates the learnings from the literature, acquires and advisors.  
 
In figure 2, the conceptual operational due diligence framework is proposed. 
The core of an operational due diligence is to provide the acquire with sufficient knowledge as to 
whether the target company should be acquired or not, which is illustrated as the center of the 
framework. To answer the core question, the acquirer needs to obtain a profound understanding of 
current and future risks and potentials concerning the target company. The next layer represent three 
independent drivers for understanding the state of the target company, namely scalability, maturity 
and synergies. The organizational scope of the operational due diligence follows the general 
definition of supply chain (Grebey, 2012). These elements are framed by the operational determinants 
in their respective groups. 
 
==PAGE:76==
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
76 
 
76 
 
Figure 2: Conceptual Operational Due Diligence Framework 
 
The operational determinant groups are supported with the following defined questions: 
● Planning, Efficiency & Quality: To what extend are strategic and operational planning 
performed consistently and effectively, and how efficiently are activities and processes 
executed, while maintaining a sufficient quality level? 
● Technology & IT System: To what degree are IT systems and technology utilized and up to 
date with industry standards? 
● Politics & Regulations: Are there any restriction, approvals or certifications that influence 
the operating model? 
● People & Organization: To what extend does the organizational setup and the employees 
support the development of company? 
● Cost & Capital: What drives the cost structure and how is capital allocated? 
● Data & Documentation: To what degree are processes and activities documented and 
generating sufficient, relevant and correct data? 
 
From an application perspective the practitioner, advisor or acquire, should start by formulating 
a set of initial hypotheses, based on the operational determinants from the framework. During the 
initial hypotheses generation, it is recommended to use the three independent drivers as indicators of 
where the operational due diligence should focus. This helps narrow down the scope of the 
assessments, which supports the often time pressured process. 
 
 
==PAGE:77==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
77 
Discussion 
Two significant elements characterized the extant literature in totality. 1) the depth and 2) the quantity 
of the extant literature was immensely scarce. On basis of the review, it is concluded that the area of 
operational due diligence is considered to have a large research gap. However, by supplementing the 
literature review with interviews of both company acquires and operational M&A advisors, it enabled 
a conceptual operational due diligence framework to be developed.  
The operational due diligence framework, intends to establish the initial foundation on where to 
focus resources and hereby achieve the most effective assessment of a target company. However, the 
framework requires extensive experience from the practitioners within the field of operations 
management and a solid foundation of financial understanding to reach full potential. In addition, the 
conceptual framework facilitates the preliminary scope, but the majority of the final results is 
subsequently gained through in-depth analysis of quantitative and qualitative data.  
 
The expert interview analysis indicated that operational due diligence are highly case specific. 
This finding questions the validity of having a generic framework. Nonetheless, the literature and 
experts underline the importance of having a strong point of origin to establish a structured due 
diligence process and achieve a successful result.  
 
Conclusion 
This paper aimed at identifying the operational determinants influencing the acquisition decision and 
structure these in a novel framework for the benefit of the acquirers and advisors. To identify these, 
a literature review was conducted and several expert interviews were organized to gather sufficient 
information. An explorative research approach of the extant literature established a contemporary 
understanding of the operational due diligence drivers. However, the extant literature is characterized 
as fragmented and incomprehensive and to counteract these limitations multiple interviews with both 
acquires and advisors were conducted. In the comparing of the outcome data a high correlation 
between the extant literature and the interviews was found, even though the depth of the literature 
was scarce. Finally, this led to an identification of 27 operational determinants which helps strengthen 
the acquisition decision from operational perspective. 
Conclusively, this paper introduces a conceptual framework for operational due diligence in 
merger and acquisition. The framework provides practitioners with a novel structure to establish the 
opening set of hypothesis that will focus the operational due diligence in the most optimal direction. 
With an increasing focus on the operational aspect of mergers and acquisitions, the importance having 
a structured approach becomes more even more essential.

Mathias Haubjerg

ABSTRACT 
An operational due diligence is characterized by a short timeline and the need for expert 
knowledge. These two aspects have a tremendous influence on both the acquisition decision and 
the overall success of an merger and acquisition (M&A). Consequently, a profound assessment 
of a target company’s operational potentials and risks held against the future performance 
expectations is considered pivotal. However, this theme is to a great extent unexplored in extant 
literature. This paper describes both qualitative and quantitative operational factors influencing 
the acquisition decision in the operational due diligence phase of a M&A. 
 
 
INTRODUCTION 
In the last five years, mergers and acquisitions (M&A) has increased, although the overall 
success rate have been inferior (Institute of Mergers, Acquisitions and Alliances, 2016). 
Therefore, it is essential to identify the target company’s operational drivers as they contribute 
to M&A success (Herd, 2004). Increasing complexity and dependency in a target company’s 
operating model, such as distribution networks, supplier relations and IT systems, continue to 
become more important to identify and understand (Malik, 2011).  
Traditionally, the legal and financial due diligence have been the main focus in the M&A 
due diligence process (Grebey, 2012). These due diligences provide insights in obligations, 
contracts, cash flow, assets, financial statements, etc. but omit the operational aspects 
(Shaughnessy, 2009). Neglecting or deprioritizing the operational assessment can prompt vital 
consequences, such as unforeseen delivery issues, for the acquisition. The operational insights 
have multiple influence points such as the valuation of the target company, leverage in price 
negotiations, the integration process, and the improvement potentials (Herd, 2004).  
The aim of this paper is to explore the operational drivers influencing the acquisition of a 
target company. Furthermore, this paper aims to structure the drivers into a normative 
framework that supports the operational M&A advisors in performing an effective operational 
due diligence, while providing acquirers with well-informed and deliberate decision foundation 
prior to the acquisition.  
This paper uses the expression operational factor as a component influencing the target 
company’s operating model in either a positively or negatively way. In addition, a simplified 
==PAGE:80==
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
80 
 
80 
definition of Grebey (2012)’s organizational scope of an operational due diligence is applied. It 
includes Sourcing, Manufacturing, Distribution, and Logistics. 
 
 
METHODOLOGY 
Due to the complex nature of the research aim, a qualitative approach is used to provide rich 
and in-depth data. The explorative approach of the study allows for thorough understanding of 
the research area. Therefore, the case-study approach is the most appropriate research 
methodology (Yin, 2013).  
 
To get insight into the M&A practitioners’ experience and obtain more detailed and in-
depth data, semi-structured interviews were conducted with several practitioners, both acquirers 
and advisors. The acquirers were chosen based on set of key parameters including (i) having 
experience with acquiring international companies, (ii) being part of multiple operational due 
diligence cases, and (iii) acquired companies with a production of physical goods and a supply 
chain. The advisors were also selected based on a set of key parameters including (i) having 
performed more than three operational due diligences, (ii) having financial insights, and (iii) 
deep operational expertise within the supply chain. Furthermore, both practitioner roles argue 
that a better understanding of the operational due diligence process is crucial. Collectively, 11 
interviews were conducted with five acquirer interviews and six operational M&A advisor 
interviews. In total, the interviewees have conducted more than 120 operational due diligence 
projects. 
  
The research is divided into four key phases. Firstly, an extensive literature review of research 
papers and industry publications were conducted. The number of articles identified in the initial 
research counted 131. Through a screening process, with a range of exclusion criteria’s including 
a) Cultural Due Diligence, b) Hedge Fund Operational Due Diligence b) Technical Due Diligence, 
the number of articles was reduced to 42. Furthermore, a detailed examination of the remaining 
articles led to a final list of 22 articles. Secondly, semi-structured interviews with several M&A 
practitioners were conducted and the qualitative data was analyzed by coding and subsequent 
a factor frequency analysis. Thirdly, structured comparison of the literature and the empirical 
data was completed. The last and forth phase concern the development of a normative 
framework that supports the acquirers and advisors in performing an operational due diligence.  
 
The data and information used for this paper were collected from acquirers’ and advisors’ 
previous experience with operational due diligence cases as a part of an M&A process. The 
research team worked in close collaboration with the advisors, as they function as the executing 
part of the operational due diligence. The semi-structured interviews provided key insights in 
analysis and the practicalities of an operational due diligence. Combined with the literature 
review, this method enabled triangularity between the extant literature and the empirical data, 
hence strengthening the validity. 
 
 
LITERATURE REVIEW 
The extant literature proposes a value chain perspective to assess the target company’s 
operational setup (Recardo, 2014). This approach helps comprehending the individual elements 
of the supply chain and it helps mitigate the risk of disregarding essential insights in the 
operating model. Grebey (2012) compartmentalize the organizational scope of the operational 
due diligence into six functional areas. The respective areas are 1) R&D, 2) Sourcing & 
Procurement, 3) Manufacturing, 4) Warehousing & Inventory, 5) Transport & Logistics, and 6) 
Sales & Marketing. The organizational scope of the operational due diligence is in this paper a 
limited version of this definition, as R&D and Sales & Marketing are excluded as shown in Figure 
1. 
 
==PAGE:81==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
81 
 
Figure 1: Operational Due Diligence Scope 
 
To identify the theoretical operational factors within the operational due diligence, a 
comprehensive analysis of the extant literature has been conducted. Generally, the literature 
categorizes the factors into six groups. These groups include 18 operational factors collectively 
and each factor is considered to have a significant impact on the acquisition decision. Table 1 
displays the resulting operational factors found through the literature review.

Even though the literature presents a scarce amount of information on operational due diligence, 
it was possible to identify a sufficient amount of operational factors concerning the operating 
model of a target company. 
 
EMPIRICAL FINDINGS 
To obtain more rich and qualitative data several interviews were organized with both acquirers 
and operational M&A advisors. A coding and a frequency analysis of the interviews enabled a 
quantification and identification of the operational factors and their relative importance. 
Furthermore, the analysis subsequently supports the development of a normative framework. 
The coding identified 222 operational factors accentuated in the empirical data. Through several 
iterations, the individual factors were evaluated and consolidated if equivalent interpretation 
occurred. Throughout the analysis, duplicates and substituting factors were eliminated. The 
analysis reduced the number of factors from 222 to 27 operational factors. To assess the 
importance, the operational factors were scored by their mentioning frequency across the 
interviews. The factors are grouped based on similarity and context, and listed in Table 2 ranked 
after highest frequency first.

The operational factor group Cost & Capital is the most frequently occurring across all 
interviewees, which emphasizes the necessity of assessing the target company’s cost structure. 
Furthermore, the operational factor Net Working Capital is in immense focus, due to the 
importance of understanding the cash conversion cycle and opportunities to free up cash. 
Another operational factor group, with relatively high focus is the group Planning, Efficiency & 
Quality, which includes the more classical operations elements. These underlying factors are 
generally underlined as having significant potential for operational improvement by several of 
the interviewees. The group Politics & Regulations received the overall lowest attention even 
==PAGE:83==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
83 
though some interviewees mentioned the factor Approvals & Certification as being a potential 
deal breaker, hence it is critical for the final acquisition decision. However, it was simultaneously 
concluded that this factor is highly case dependent and appears infrequently. 
 
Generally, the majority of interviewees consider a common approach with two high level 
perspectives for the operational due diligence. Firstly, a risk perspective and secondly an 
improvement potential perspective. These two perspectives help clarify key insights to in the 
pre-acquisition process, since they help quantify the return on investment, mitigate uncertainty, 
prevent unexpected post-acquisition investments, etc.  
In addition, two guiding factors with distinctive character were mentioned by multiple 
interviewees. The factors intersect the entire supply chain and several of the previously defined 
factor groups, namely the target company’s ability to scale and its maturity. As these two factors 
support the holistic picture of the company they are denoted as highly important to incorporate 
as part of the operational due diligence. For example, the procurement process’s maturity level 
and the ability to scale the production output are two ways of understanding the target company. 
Two other and more case-specific factors that were mentioned in the interviews are consolidation 
and synergies. These are highly influenced by interlinkages and often only considered in merger 
cases.  
 
Ultimately, all interviewees consider the operational due diligence’s organizational scope 
as 
the 
supply 
chain, 
separated 
into 
components 
as 
Sourcing 
& 
Procurement, 
Manufacturing/Production, Warehouse & Distribution, and Logistics & Transport. 
 
COMPARATIVE ANALYSIS 
When comparing the extant literature and the empirical data, a noticeable correlation is 
apparent. However, where the literature only addresses the subjects superficial, the empirical 
data are much more detailed and practically oriented in the description of the operational due 
diligence. The incomprehensive theory falls short in the level of detail and research quantity 
within the subject of operational due diligence. Furthermore, the empirical data provides several 
additional operational factors and more depth, which fortify the purpose of the research in this 
paper on operational due diligence.  
One of the major differences is the maturity factor, which is almost non-existing in the 
extant literature. The interviewees use this as a metric for quantifying the current state of the 
target company’s operating model. This factor cut across multiple operational factors and is 
expressed as being vital instrument for the operational due diligence.  
Both the extant literature and the empirical data point to the significance of 
understanding a target company’s People & Organization. However, the interviewees distinguish 
between the workforce competencies and the executive leadership competencies, while the 
extant literature presents a more holistic perspective. In addition, the empirical data supplement 
the literature with several operations management factors to be incorporated in an operational 
due diligence context, among these are Operational Planning, Efficiency & Flow, Quality 
Management, etc. 
Generally, the literature does not include information on where to find data or which 
analysis that needs to be conducted. Therefore, the empirical data were crucial in order to obtain 
more knowledge about the individual factors, which is necessary to develop a normative 
framework for the operational due diligence process. 
 
A NORMATIVE OPERATIONAL DUE DILIGENCE FRAMEWORK 
A common characteristic in the extant literature and the interviews is the recommendation of 
utilizing a structured approach when performing a operational due diligence. The strict timeline 
during operational due diligence process require a simple approach driven by factors and include 
iterations. Conclusively, an efficient and comprehensive procedure is proposed as a normative 
hypothesis driven framework with knowledge from both literature and practitioners. 
In figure 2, a framework incorporating findings from literature and expert interviews are 
is presented. The framework helps identify important insights influencing the acquisition decision 
through operational key questions and associated analyses. 
==PAGE:84==
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
84 
 
84

==PAGE:85==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
85 
To set the acquirer in an optimal position before the final negotiation, the acquirer must 
have comprehensive insight in the target company’s current and future risks and potentials. The 
framework builds on six swim lanes, each with an operational factor group. The individual swim 
lanes contain key questions that addresses the operational factors in the supply chain. To answer 
these key questions and obtain the right data on target company, a proposed analysis is 
associated to each question. The list only contains the primary analysis and are not an exhaustive 
list. Consequently, the practitioner needs to ensure the analysis are in context to the case. As a 
supplement, the practitioner should assess the target company in terms of maturity and its 
ability to scale. 
In the operational due diligence process, the practitioners must balance obtain data from 
multiple sources in order to gain sufficient understanding of the target company’s operating 
model. Typically, two situations occur either 1) scarce amount of data or 2) data abundance. It 
is crucial for the practitioners to obtain the right data through the right source. The framework 
assists the practitioners in selecting the right question, while the data are available from five 
sources: 
● 
Publicly available data/information such as financial statements, news articles, press 
releases, etc. – Often used in the early stage of the due diligence to get an initial 
understanding of the target company. 
● 
Investor memorandums and management presentations – The first information received 
from the target company. Valuable data that often are used as foundation for the 
hypothesis. 
● 
Site visits – The practitioners normally have access to one site visit per site in the due 
diligence process. This is a crucial part of process, since it provide deep insight in the 
production setup, flow, culture, etc. 
● 
Interviews – There are typically one or more Q&A sessions either through psysical 
interviews or via telephone. This data source pose an opportunity to get answers to key 
questions and assess the target company’s people competencies. 
● 
Data room (data requests & questions to management and/or staff) – Data is available 
in the data room. But often is it irrelevant, redundant and overloaded. Therefore is it 
important to request specific information to perform analyses or answer questions. 
 
Finally, based on information and data received from the five sources, the primary analyses can 
be performed. The analyses are an instrument to confirm or reject the hypothesis, and the 
results hereof function as a powerful aid in the final negotiation and acquisition decision. 
 
DISCUSSION 
The extant literature suffers from a large research gap. Both the depth and the quantity of 
operational due diligence theory are immensely scarce. Hence qualitative data consisting of 
interviews with both acquirers and operational M&A advisors are crucial to obtain a sufficient 
understanding of the target company’s operating model. While the literature recommends a 
structured approach, no theoretical framework exists. The research contributes to the literature 
with a structural approach and are the foundation to an effective and thorough operational 
assessment process. However, the interviewees express that obtaining full benefit of the 
framework, require that the team, allocated to the operational due diligence, have competent 
proficiency and experience within operations management and possess a solid financial 
understanding.  
Since the operational due diligence cases are characterized by being case specific, a 
generic framework functionality can be questioned. Nonetheless, the importance of having a 
strong point of origin and a structured approach are expressed in both the theory and the 
empirical data. Hence, the framework accommodates the need for a structured approach to excel 
operational due diligences. 
 
CONCLUSION 
The aim of this paper was to investigate the operational factors influencing the success of M&As. 
To achieve this, the operational factors were identified and structure them in a normative 
==PAGE:86==
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
86 
 
86 
framework to develop a solid basis and guideline for conducting a successful operational due 
diligence. A comprehensive literature review was performed and supported with 11 interviews 
with acquirers and advisors. While the explorative literature review established a foundation for 
the understanding of operational factors, the semi-structured interviews provided more 
comprehensive and thorough knowledge of both the data gathering process, the operational 
drivers, key questions and finally, analyses, which collectively provide an approach to the 
operational due diligence. 
In total, 27 operational factors were identified based on the consolidation of extant 
literature and empirical data. Each operational factor is expressed with a key question to help 
the practitioner identify the target company’s risks and potentials. 
Conclusively, a normative framework for supporting the practitioners in the operational 
due diligence process was presented. The framework creates a foundation for hypothesis 
development and helps focus on the most important key questions that need to be answered. 
With increasing merger and acquisition activity and growing complexity in supply chains, a 
normative framework supporting the time pressured process of operational due diligence is more 
important than ever.

Appendix C.1 – General Interviews Information 
Unsolicited E-mails to M&A Practitioners 
 
Hi, 
 
I am currently writing my master thesis at DTU Engineering Management, with the aim of 
Developing an Operational Due Diligence Framework for Mergers & Acquisitions. Hence, I am 
looking for individuals with experience from conducting operational due diligences to help provide 
some insights.  
 
As interviewee you do not have to prepare anything, the interview will be based on your 
experience. Furthermore, the interviewee is not intended to divulge business sensitive information 
such as current framework, client details or the like. Instead the interviewees should only provide 
information about their previous ODD experiences.  
 
--------------------------------------------------- More details ------------------------------------------------- 
 
Background 
The thesis project is a part of DTU Management Engineering, with supervision from Zaza Nadja 
Lee Herbert-Hansen. Furthermore, the thesis is written together with Chris Berg Porsgaard, who is 
also a student at DTU. Currently, a literature review has been conducted to identify the existing 
material/frameworks for performing operational due diligences (ODD). However, the research 
revealed a very limited amount of information on the topic. 
 
Next step 
The coming thesis research incorporates 12 to 15 interviews of 1-hour duration. The interviewees 
are split into two different groups: (1) consultants/partners who have conducted operational due 
diligences, (2) individuals from either a private equity firm or an internal M&A department at a 
larger corporation. The findings will subsequently be validated with a survey with the aim of 
quantifying the operational determinants impacting the decision of acquiring another company.  
 
Final Outcome 
We have been fortunate enough to get accepted to present our thesis at the conference, The 
European Operations Management Association. Furthermore, the aim is to publish the framework 
as an article in the Journal of International Management  
 
What do you gain 
If you like, we will make a presentation with the findings and send you the presentation afterwards. 
This will hopefully give you new inputs to the way you are conducting ODD’s.

Appendix C.3 – Guideline for Consultant Interview 
Consultant Interview 
Briefing 
Background 
This interview is a part of our master thesis, which is conducted in collaboration with DTU 
Management Engineering and with supervision from Assistant Professor Zaza Nadja Lee Herbert-
Hansen. 
Purpose 
The number of mergers and acquisitions (M&As) has over the last five years increased greatly 
(Institute of Mergers, Acquisitions and Alliances, 2016). Furthermore, 93% of private equity 
professionals point to operational performance gains to drive an acquisition decision and attribute 
cost reductions as the most important lever for value creation, after a private equity firm acquires a 
company (Roberts et al., 2016). However, the overall success rate of M&A activity remains low and 
the approach to understand an acquisition target’s operating model remains non-exhaustive and 
unstandardized.  
 
With this thesis we investigate the pivotal determinants for assessing operational performance and 
identifying improvement potentials in an acquisition target. A literature review has been conducted 
and it revealed a research gap within the field. Therefore, we are arranging these interviews to gain 
insights in what the best practise of ODD is.  
 
Scope 
The thesis focuses on firms that produce physical goods, have a global or European footprint, and 
are privately held. Governmental and non-profit organizations, and firms operating in the service 
sector, are therefore out of scope. 
Goal 
Based on practitioners experiences and the literature the aim is to build a generic operational due 
diligence framework, that ensure a structured approach to handle ODD in the best manner.  
Agenda/Process 
The agenda of the interview are based on four main subjects, namely: Personal Background, ODD 
Assessment, ODD Process and Post-acquisition.

Appendix C.4 – PE Interviews Information 
 
E-mails to Private Equity Firms 
 
______________________________ Thesis Details ____________________________ 
  
Title: The Key to Successful Operational Due Diligence in Mergers & Acquisitions 
  
Background 
The master thesis is written by Mathias Haubjerg and Chris Berg Porsgaard and it is a part of DTU 
Management Engineering with supervision from Assistant Professor Zaza Nadja Lee Herbert-Hansen. 
  
Purpose & description 
The number of mergers and acquisitions has over the last five years increased greatly. 93% of private equity 
professionals point to operational performance gains to drive an acquisition decision and attribute cost 
reductions as the most important lever for value creation. However, the overall success rate of M&A activity 
remains low and the approach to understand an acquisition target’s operating model remains an unexplored 
research area. 
  
The purpose of the thesis is therefore to identify the key drivers to a successful operational due diligence 
(ODD) and subsequently investigate how knowledge from the ODD can be utilized to excel value creation in 
the post-acquisition phase. The research process is split into three parts, namely (A) literature review (B) 
interviews and (C) a survey. 
  
A.  analysis of existing literature related to operational due diligence in M&A based on 131 investigated 
articles. 
B.  builds on knowledge obtained through interview with two primary sources (1) ODD advisors and (2) 
private equity firms and internal M&A teams in larger corporations. (Your contribution) 
C. is used to quantify the identified operational determinants which have been identified in both the initial 
literature review and the interviews. 
  
Outcome 
The primary objective of the master thesis project is to contribute to better understanding the key drivers to a 
successful operational due diligence and hereby overall success rate of M&As. It is believed that through a 
structured analysis of both existing literature and industry knowledge, a practical and useful framework and 
approach to perform operational due diligence can be identified. Furthermore, the findings and final 
framework will be presented at the European Operations Management Association's yearly conference in 
Edinburgh, UK. Lastly, the aim is to publish an article in one of the leading management journal. 
  
What do you gain? 
Besides contributing with an interview to the research, we would gladly provide you with our final article 
and give you a presentation of the findings. This can help you as a PE firm to: 
  
·        Drive more effective and comprehensive due diligences 
·        Get insights on where to focus the due diligence efforts in the operations 
·        … and potentially help establish a more precise target valuation. 
 
 
==PAGE:97==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
97 
Appendix C.5 – Guideline for Consultant Interview 
 
Private Equity Interview 
Briefing 
Background 
This interview is a part of our master thesis, which is conducted in collaboration with DTU 
Management Engineering and with supervision from Assistant Professor Zaza Nadja Lee Herbert-
Hansen. 
Purpose 
The number of mergers and acquisitions (M&As) has over the last five years increased greatly 
(Institute of Mergers, Acquisitions and Alliances, 2016). Furthermore, 93% of private equity 
professionals point to operational performance gains to drive an acquisition decision and attribute 
cost reductions as the most important lever for value creation, after a private equity firm acquires a 
company (Roberts et al., 2016). However, the overall success rate of M&A activity remains low and 
the approach to understand an acquisition target’s operating model remains non-exhaustive and 
unstandardized.  
 
With this thesis we investigate the pivotal determinants for assessing operational performance and 
identifying improvement potentials in an acquisition target. A literature review has been conducted 
and it revealed a research gap within the field. Therefore, we are arranging these interviews to gain 
insights in what the best practise of ODD is.  
 
Scope 
The thesis focuses on firms that produce physical goods, have a global or European footprint, and 
are privately held. Governmental and non-profit organizations, and firms operating in the service 
sector, are therefore out of scope. 
Goal 
Based on practitioners experiences and the literature the aim is to build a generic operational due 
diligence framework, that ensure a structured approach to handle ODD in the best manner.  
Agenda/Process 
The agenda of the interview are based on four main subjects, namely: Personal Background, ODD 
Assessment, ODD Process and Post-acquisition. 
- 
No names due to confidentiality 
- 
the interviewer role will remain passive and let the interviewee speak to avoid bias. 
 
==PAGE:98==
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
98 
 
98 
Questions 
Personal and Background 
 
 1. What is your experience with Operational Due Diligence? 
 
 2. How many ODDs have you been involved in? 
 
 3. What was your role in a typical ODD (active role, steering role) 
 
 4. Have you performed ODD’s related to both integration (buy and build) and 
standalone?  
 
 5. Who is performing the ODD’s (third party or in-house)? 
 
 6. Do you have and do you use a structured approach/framework?  
 
 7. Which competencies are you looking for when selecting third party (availability, 
industry, expertise)? 
 
 8. Why and why not do you perform ODD’s? (please elaborate - the importance of it) 
 
 9. 
 How important do you consider ODD compared to the other DD’s? 
 
 10.  How often do you merge or acquire without performing ODD? 
 
 
ODD Assessment  
“What are the operational determinants influencing the acquisition decision for acquiring 
firms in the due diligence phase?” 
 
 
11. Which functional areas (organizational scope) do you consider when conducting an 
ODD? 
 
 
12. What do you expect to be the outcome of an ODD? 
 
 
13.  What do you use the outcome of the ODD to? 
o   Related to buy/not buy and related to 100days plan 
 
 
14. Where do you typically put most focus and why (e.g. your last ODD)? 
 
15. Do you define a set of key questions/hypothesis to be covered in the ODD? 
 
 
16. How do you identify these key questions and are they connected to investment 
rationale? 
 
 
17. Are there some general hypothesises you use, if so please list the most generic ones?  
 
 
18. What data  point / information do you request/want out of the ODD  
(Net working capital (DIO, DSO, DPO), Capex, Opex, etc.)  
 
 
19. Follow up: How should/could these data points be delivered to accommodate 
acquisition decision and the valuation model 
 
 
20. What outcomes from an ODD could potentially help you generate a more clear 
valuation? and more well-founded investment decision? 
 
 
21. What do you experience as being the most important key take away? 
 
 
22. What do you see as the most important operational M&A risk? 
 
==PAGE:99==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
99 
 
23. What do you typically see as being considered as “red flags”/”deal breaker”? 
 
 
24. Follow-up:  Definition of “ Green, yellow and red flags”/”deal breakers”? 
 
 
25. Do you consider the target company's maturity in your assessment? 
 
 
26. Are there other elements that are important in the assessment? 
 
 
27.  Which factors determine the decision of whether to buy or not to buy? 
 
 
28. Which metrics are most important to make the buy/not buy decision? 
 
 
ODD Process 
“What is the optimal process and timeline for carrying out the operational due diligence 
phase?”

32. Explain the importance of the steps

34. How do you interact with the ODD performing firm? 
 
35. How often during an ODD do you typically have contact to the consultancies (Daily, 
weekly etc.)? 
 
 
36. What expectations do you have to the consultancies? 
 
 
37. What would make this process/interaction better? 
 
 
38. How is alignment ensured between the acquire and the advisor? 
 
 
39. How much do you interact with the simultaneously performed DDs (Financial, 
Legal, Commercial etc.) 
 
40. What would help you perform a better ODD?  
 
 
41. What do you considers a successful ODD? 
 
 
42. Other final comments you would like us to take away from this interview? 
 
 
Post-Acquisition 
“How are the insights identified in operational due diligence used to excel value creation in 
the post-acquisition phase?” 
 
 
43. How do you experience that the information from the ODD are used in the post-
acquisition phase? 
 
 
44. How do you think ODD insights could be utilized even more in the post-acquisition 
phase?

Appendix D: Survey Questionnaire 
Appendix D.1 – Survey Questionaire Information 
Unsolicited E-mails to M&A Practitioners 
 
Research on Operational Due Diligence Framework 
 
Hi, 
 
We are two students from the Technical University of Denmark that currently write our master 
thesis together. The dissertation addresses the subject operational due diligence (ODD), and aims at 
exploring the operational determinants that influence the acquisition decision in an Merger & 
Acquisition. Furthermore, the objective is to develop a framework based on the discovered 
determinants, which will function as a supporting tool for practitioners in the ODD process. 
  
Until now, we have reviewed the extant literature and interviewed practitioners, both acquires and 
advisors. Based on the obtained information this survey has been developed. The intention with the 
survey is to reach more people, and hereby attain enough mass to draw conclusions upon the 
results. Furthermore, the aim is to receive more detailed information such as analyses conducted 
during the ODD process. 
  
If you have any experience with operational due diligence or the operational (supply chain) part of a 
commercial due diligence, we will be pleased to have your response on our survey. The survey 
takes approximately 15 minutes. 
  
Please feel free to share this survey with your colleagues or other individuals with ODD experience. 
Thanks in advance.  
 
Link to the Survey: https://goo.gl/forms/6iyKrZ0MFJN51Z5O2

Appendix E.2 – Consultant Transcribed Interviews 
Consultant Interview 
Interviewer(s): Mathias Haubjerg (MH) & Chris Porsgaard (C) 
Interviewee(s): Managing Consultant (M) 
Date: 27-03-2017 
Duration: 52,00 minutes 
Language: Danish 
  
Chris Briefer (0.00 -01.30)  
C: Operationel Due Diligence (ODD), hvor mange vil du skyde på du har været involveret i gennem 
tiden?  
 
M: Det er jo meget svært spørgsmål, fordi jeg laver også mange Due Diligence, hvor vi kigger på 
lidt af det hele for mange store virksomheder, men egentlig projekter hvor vi laver rigtig due 
diligence er det nok ikke mere end 10 styk. 
  
C: Cool, hvilken rolle har du typisk haft, når du har været en del af det?  
 
M: De sidste mange har jeg været projektleder på  
 
C: Cool, de ODD du har været en del af det, er det kun stand-alone cases eller er det også merger?  
 
M: Jeg har kun lavet en som var en industriel aquisition, fordi jeg primært arbejder med PE fonde, 
så det er ikke så meget med merger. Så en ud af de ti har været en merger  
 
C: Når du arbejder som projektleder, har du så et framework eller en approach som du bruger 
struktureret?  
 
M: Ja det gør vi, det er standardiseret, og man kan sige meget forsimplet sagt, så er det et spørgsmål 
om at kigge på to overordnet temaer, hvor det ene det klassiske tema, hvor vi kigger på alle 
nøgleelementer i værdikæden, altså sourcing og selve produktionen, hvor effektiv den er og 
hvordan den er sat sammen og logistiksiden, og hvad er er det for nogle, hvordan er det 
kapitalsituationen ser ud og en helhedsbetragtning på det hele, sådan hurtigt fortalt. Den anden er 
meget relateret til de strukturelle strategiske elementer, som enten kan være drevet af købers 
dagsorden lidt om der har ønsker på nogle af elementerne, men det kan også være strukturelle 
forbedringsmuligheder der er for f.eks. du køber en ikke særlig god virksomhed, der har produktion 
i Danmark, hvordan ser businesscasen ud i og lave om i det setup strategisk, der er nogle inden for 
det operationelle område, som vi kalder strategiske sammenlægninger, skal vi virkelige producere 
det her selv i fremtiden? Skal vi flytte dele af vores produktion ud til lavprislande i stedet for. Et 
eller andet uanset det overordnet split, det er ligesom der hvor vi begynder at gå på toppen af det. 
Det er normalt de to, der er vores hovedårer 
  
C: Det giver rigtig god mening, det bevæger os ned i, du svarer selv på det, men jeg runder lige 
igen, det første er netop også et spørgsmål om det organisatoriske scope for, for at vurdere, du 
typisk begiver dig ud. Nu sagde du selv det var sourcing, produktion, warehouse eller noget 
distribution, det er også det vi selv ser i litteraturen, vi er startet med at lave et litteratur review og 
fandt ud af, at der var ikke særlig meget på det, men det der så var, det var så det som du også 
==PAGE:143==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
143
nævner at man kigger på supply chainen og det operationelle, og så er der så nogle der også 
karakteriserer det som, der kan også være noget salgsorganisation ind over, det er også noget 
service 
 
M: Nåh ja, men selvfølgelig det er også inde over supply chain’en  
 
C: Lige præcis, men fokus i det her, det er meget også supply chain for det her framework vi 
fokuserer på, så på den måde giver det rigtig god mening det du siger. I forhold til når du kigger på 
de her områder for supply chain, er der så nogle områder, du ligger mere vægt på end andre?  
 
M: Det er svært at sige, man kan jo gå et skridt tilbage og sige hvad er det for et formål vi går ud 
med? Så skal man jo virkeligheden kigge på investorens business case og så sige hvad er det for 
nogel value drivers der er i forhold til det, hvad er det for nogle ting, vi skal adressere i forhold til 
køb. For der er både nogle ting, som er forbedringspotentialer som gør at prisen kan blive bedre, 
fordi vi kan gøre en masse ting, så det er meget bredt, i virkeligheden vil jeg sige det hele. Man kan 
sige en private equity fond vil altid være interesseret i at frigøre kapital, så det med network capital 
det skal vi kigge på, men der er jo ligeså meget i at sige, hvad er det for nogle 
forbedringspotentialer, der er i at være mere effektiv og det kan være i alle mulige ting, så vi kan få 
det ind i vores evalueringsmodel, så vi kan få en bedre case, når vi skal ud at købe, så jeg vil 
egentlig sige, jeg tror svaret vil sige nej, det kan man ikke sige. Overordnet vil jeg sige nej.    
 
C: Det giver fint mening. Cool. Måden vores spørgsmål er stillet op det er sådan, vi starter med 
scope det er sådan organisatorisk og funktionelt og så det næste spørgsmål er, er der nogle key 
qestions eller hypoteser, som går igen, og hvad er de i så fald, når du vurdere.  
 
M: Uha, hmm hehe  
 
C: Nej det skal ikke være nemt  
 
M: Nej, det ved jeg godt, men det er bare for ikke at gentage for meget, det ligeså meget det. Det er 
der selvfølgelig, det er jo typisk et spørgsmål om at risikoafdække, evt. se på køber og ting, som 
man ikke har været opmærksom på. Men altså lavt modenhed er ikke nødvendigvis dårlig for køber, 
hvis de kan lave et, hvis de kan forbedre prisen, så det er jo sådan lidt underligt, at et dårligt resultat 
kan i princippet godt være en okay ting, hvis der er noget, en lækkerbisken man kan gøre en masse 
ting ud af, så det er sådan lidt en underlig situation, men hvad er det for nogle hovedhypoteser vi 
kigger på, der kan man jo løbe alle områder igennem, men en hovedhypotese kunne være, jamen 
sourcing, lav modenhed vi køber ned ad gaden i stedet for at bruge en god global sourcing, vi har 
brugt for mange leverandører på det forskellige, en helt klassisk analyse af hvordan det er fordelt. 
Helt klassisk hypotese vi har for meget lager, vi er forsigtige med hvor meget vi har på, fordi det er 
en vækstcase, så det er typisk, at de ikke er fokuseret nok på det. Produktivitetsforbedringer i 
produktionen er også en standard hypotese, hvad kan vi gøre der? En af de ting jeg ikke nævnte i 
starten omkring temaer er jo også i forhold til scalability er også klart en af hovedtemaerne vi 
kigger på, en af de mere strategiske ting vi kigger på skalerbarheden i virksomheden, hvad er det for 
nogle capex ting der ligger (9.55). Er der nogle capex ting i fremtiden som ikke belyst ordentlig 
eller ligger der nogle buttleneck som skal investeres i for at kunne sætte vækst, som de har planlagt. 
Det er nok de typiske. 
 
==PAGE:144==
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
144 
 
144 
C: Det er super, det er lige det her vi er på udkig efter også for at høre sådan næste spørgsmål 
tager lige skridtet dybere, hvad er det for nogle analyser, som, du har lidt allerede været inde på 
det i forhold til networking capital eksempelvis, til at belyse, men endelige bare blive ved er der 
nogle analyser, som du tænker sådan, hvis vi nu tager de der funktionelle områder eksempelvis 
capital networking, er der andre du kan komme på som konkrete analyser? 
 
M: Det er jo sjovt det her med operationel, fordi måske skulle man starte med at sige at meget af det 
vi gør er jo også vores ekspertise og vores erfaringer og gå ud og se tingene og meget hurtigt danne 
sig et indtryk af hvilket niveau det er på og kommunikere det, det er jo grunden til at det hele ikke 
bare er sat på flasker, så jeg vil jo starte med at sige, at analyserne er jo, der er nogle steder, hvor de 
kan pin pointe potentialet, men der er også rigtig meget af det vi kan se bare ved at gå rundt og 
f.eks. have en snak med ledelsen og så gå rundt på fabriksgulvet og så kan man, så ved måske hvor 
vi er på vej hen, og så skal vi analysere det. Analyserne er jo tit de bekræftelser i de vurderinger 
man laver, men også måden hvor vi kan kvantificere potentialet. Og hvis jeg skal være helt ærlig 
mange analyserne, det er meget sjældent jeg gør det, det er hvert fald mange år siden lang jeg har 
gjort det, og jeg laver dem ikke særlig tit selv den gang, men man kan sige, networking capital, man 
kan sige det er jo, alt det der, det er noget med nogle coverage analyser på varenumre, 
lagerbindinger på forskellige steder og det er jo sådan en end to end analyser, hvad er lead time og 
niveauet, så det typisk noget med at finde ud af noget med nogle benchmarks, hvad gør andre i 
samme branche, hvad kan vi finde ud af? Hvad er det for nogle niveauer vi ligger på? Hvad er det vi 
har erfaringer med i forhold til operational.  
På sourcing og procurement siden er det typisk en vurdering af hvordan leverandørerne er fordelt, 
især i kategorier, hvor ligger det henne, hvordan er status på den kontrakt de har, altså det er jo helt 
nede på det detaljeniveau, for at finde ud af, hvornår er den sidst blevet genforhandlet, er det fordelt 
på nogle stykker sådan lidt tilfældigt, er det nogle der ligger tæt på eller ej, har de været ude i et 
større udbud helt ned på det niveau, kan vi gøre noget? Vi køber motoren lidt længere ned af gaden, 
men kunne man købe den direkte i Kina, hvis man planlagde sig lidt ud af det osv. osv. Logistik og 
distribution og sådan noget er jo mere end… igen et benchmark på hvad sådan noget bør koste, det 
er jo typisk sådan at vi bruger det gode redskab til at vurdere vi har, hvor de ligger henne, men da 
det igen bygget på en erfaring, vi har jo nogle folk, som kender det her område så godt, at man 
normalt kan tage dem med ind og sige, hvad er det for nogle aftaler vi har? Hvordan er setuppet? 
Hvordan ser det ud? Så kan vi meget hurtigt inden vi sådan finder ud af om det er gode vilkår eller 
ej, så det er jo også typisk noget vi kigger på, men også hele setuppet hvor er det lageret ligger 
henne? Hvor er det  center of gravity i forhold til hvor man har valgt at placere det. Er det fordi man 
ikke har gjort noget ved det endnu, eller er det fordi, man ikke har haft en person, som vidste at det 
var vigtigt, og at det var noget man kunne spare nogle penge på.  
På produktionen der vil det jo typisk være en blød vurdering af hvor modne de er i deres 
produktivitet, hvor meget arbejder de med redskaber, så som lean inde i produktionen, og hvor langt 
er de kommet, men det er jo en af de ting, det kan man næsten se ved at gå rundt i fabrikken, så ved 
du, hvor de er henne, og så kigge på hvilke historiske forbedringer de har lavet, hvad vil deres evne 
være til at eksekvere mere, og hvis du skruer op for den indsats hvor meget mere vil du kunne 
realisere. Sourcing, lager, sådan noget som IT kan også være rigtig vigtig i ODD, hvis det ikke er 
nogle af vores kompetencer, så har vi fået kollegaer inde som har kompetencerne, det er sådan lidt 
noget der falder mellem to stole, nogle gange laver i seperate IT ODD, men det kan være en ret 
vigtig ting f.eks. hvis de har et gammelt system eller det sådan noget der skal opgraderes, det er 
noget nu skal vi til at sælge, så må vi hellere sige, vi har en plan for hvad der skal ske med IT, og så 
kan man kigge på den plan og sige, jamen det koster tre gange så meget at gøre det de har planlagt, 
allerede der er du inde i strategi, for hvis køber skal sælge det videre til en som har deres eget IT 
==PAGE:145==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
145
system, hvorfor så overhovedet investere i det, er det ikke bedre bare lade vær, du får ingen penge 
for noget som køber ikke skal bruge. Så der er rigtig mange strategiske overvejelser, man kan sige 
nu sidder vi i øjeblikket og kigger på en case, hvor vi ved  at der er busines i to separate enheder. 
Der er rigtig mange, der er sådan specielt de der strategiske issues der dukker op, hvordan kan vi 
adresser det?  Hvordan skal den nye organisation se ud på den ene side af bordet og på den anden 
side af bordet? Hvem skal have hvilke folk, hvilke folk skal rekrutteres for at kunne drive 
operations. Når vi laver ODD, så kigger vi tit på rigtig mange ting også, altså bare hvordan skal 
finance gå, It osv.  
En anden analyse kan være hvordan er skalability ud over produktionen, så kan det også være 
staffing på overhead siden, hvor mange folk skal man være i indkøb, hvor mange disponenter skal 
der sidde? Skal vi have en forhandler mere siddende? Hvor mange skal vi være i finans? Hvor 
mange skal vi være i HR for at vi laver dobbelt så meget? Og er den plan der ligger der for 
konservativ i forhold til, hvor meget de tror det skal vokse… jeg sidder jo bare og fyrrer afsted 
 
C: Jamen det det er sindssygt godt    
 
 M: Man kan sige noget af det jeg ikke har nævnt, det er at overordnet, så vil man altid lave en eller 
anden businesscase i vores udgave en finansiel case, hvor vi på baggrund af det management fra 
virksomheden har sagt, at vi forventer det på salg siden, vi forventer at vi skal kunne gøre det for at 
kunne levere det på den operationelle side og det er, man kan sige i sidste ende, så kommer vi med 
alle mulige anbefalinger en fin rapport, og røde flag og ting der skal der skal adresseres og man skal 
være opmærksom på for at det kommer igennem investeringskomiteen men i sidste ende så er det 
den der businesscase og vores holdninger til hvordan de her omkostningsstrukturer kommer til at 
udvikle sig, er jo en af de allervigtigste ting, der giver indblik i typisk fondens vurdering.  
Ja, det er jo et ret vigtigt arbejde, og det er jo der hvor vi ligesom kommer med vores bud på alle de 
faktorer vi lige har gennemgået, hvordan kan man reducere det ene og hvor meget 
forbedringspotentiale ligger der dér. Så kan man måske sige til det, at nu sidder vi og snakker ud fra 
det i en verden, hvor køber ikke har gjort en masse forberedelsesarbejde, men det vi tit oplever er 
jo, og det vi tit gør, for de folk, der vil sælge deres virksomhed, de sætter sig jo ned og laver en plan 
for, hvad de godt vil lave på det operationelle inden de går ud af virksomheden, det vil sige de har 
ligesom forberedt hen over de næste tre år, der kan vi reducere vores indkøbsomkostninger så 
meget, og vi kan forbedre produktionen så meget osv. osv.  så vi kan faktisk blive mødt med et helt 
katalog ofte udarbejdet af en anden konsulentvirksomhed for, hvordan alle de der 
forbedringspotentialer skal se ud, og alle de der skal vi ligesom gå i gang med at analysere og det er 
et udmærket grundlag, for så har vi så noget at tage udgangspunkt i og så kan vi give vores 
vurdering på baggrund af det. Hele den her liste af initiativer, hvad tror vi på, hvad tror vi ikke på, 
og hvad glemmer man, skal man lave et helt andet? Typisk det her er planen ledelsen har givet, men 
vi kan komme ind og sige, det er hul i hovedet, og vi mener vi skal lukke det, og resten skal ned i 
Østeuropa, så laver vi assembly der. Det der drop det, det er for kompliceret, det er typisk det vi 
gør, og det også der vi helst gerne vil hen, for det er sjovere at arbejde med de der ting, så det er 
også en standard ting.  
 
C: Fedt, bare lige for at følge op på det, vi har identificeret syv elementer i litteraturen meget meget 
overordnet, som du selv lige har nævnt. Du nævner alle sammen, der er en vi ikke har snakket så 
meget om, og det er nok pga. integration, ellers snakker vi meget om people og organisationen, de 
rigtige folk, så er der forbedringerne de eksisterende forbedringer og udfordrer dem, 
skaleringselementet, IT og support og systemsupport, operations cost og assets som også er en del 
af det. Så er der noget risiko afdækning, som var det første du nævnte og så den sidste omkring 
==PAGE:146==
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework 
146 
 
146 
synergier, og det er nok også fordi du kun har haft en som var en industriel spiller, men kan du 
huske var der noget der gik igen i forhold til at i skulle kigge på?  
 
M: Nej, fordi det var i virkeligheden et konglomerat så det skulle ikke være en integreret del af en 
anden virksomhed, det var der ikke nogen planer for, så nej, men det er jo ikke svært at regne ud, 
jeg ved jo hvordan de arbejder deroppe i store virksomheder og internationale virksomheder, de har 
jo som regel nogle måltal, hvis de har gjort det nok og de har erfaring med så kan de jo sige ned til 
mindste, vi kan forvente at spare ti procent på indkøb i vores sourcing, hvis de er med på at have 
erfaring på det niveau, så der er mange af de der ting som vi kan løbe igennem, produktion der og 
der og der, ja alle vores underleverandør kan lave det i stedet for, så kan vi beholde den der 
produktion, det kommer til at være meget casebaseret, men det er klart, der er meget sådan nogle 
ting, og der to virksomheder og den ene er dobbelt så stor som den anden, ja… jeg vil sige, jeg tror 
ikke der er noget, de der temaer du nævner går på den anden led af værdikæden, vi har værdikæden 
og så har vi de der andre temaer ikke og man kan sige jamen synergi der er det jo bare at gå den vej 
igennem på den led.  
 
C: Det er fedt at høre dig sige det, for jeg kan afsløre…. Vi fik afklaret meget omkring analyse og 
hele hypotese delen og hvordan du ligesom angriber dem, vi har lidt omkring adgangen, du nævner 
brugen af forskellige datakilder og benchmark er det noget der altid indgår i hvilket omfang?  
 
 
M:  Altså man kan sige benchmark er i virkeligheden noget, som vi, nu skal jeg passe på hvad jeg 
siger, jeg tror ikke vi nødvendigvis er kæmpestore fortaler af benchmarks, fordi du ved at verden er 
kompliceret og man adskiller sig fra benchmark på de her faktorer og de er på denne her rejse, men 
man sige der jo selvfølgelig, vi vil jo godt have et andet rum for industrisegmentet, automotives 
f.eks.  der er et helt specielt form for distributions setup, som kræver en ret god leveringstid hvad 
best in class for network capital inden for det område. Det kan jo give en nedre og en øvre ramme 
måske og tale om hvilket aspekt man ligge op ad, men jeg synes altid man skal have en kvalitative 
ramme, der siger noget om, hvor synes jeg det er rimeligt med det fokus vi har, at bevæge os hen 
mod, så jeg synes tit det er et redskab, men det er også kun det der er, og det er ikke særligt meget 
mere, det superfedt at have et godt benchmark for at sanity tjekke nogle ting, men det er også det, 
der skal bare rigtig meget intelligens og erfaring ned i og bruge det… det er jo ikke en mekanisk 
øvelse, men det er klart altså.. ja.. inventory levels der kan også være noget med.. så noget som hvis 
man er på det her modnes niveau på indkøbssiden, og man har fem leverandører og korter ned til to, 
hvor meget kunne jeg så typisk spare, det er jo også et benchmark, men det er mere enten et 
erfaringsbaseret eller et literatur benchmark end det er virksomhedssammenlignings benchmark. 
Der selvfølgelige også andre måder man kan benchmarke på, det vi ofte gør, jamen kigger vi på en 
virksomhed, er laver denne her type produkter, der har vi jo efterhånden så meget erfaring, at når vi 
kigger på andre virksomheder, der laver et lignende type produkt, med forskellige former for setup 
og strukturer og løsninger, det synes jeg er meget mere interessante benchmarks. Altså prøv og hør 
de her får produceret alle deres undersamlinger hernede, plus de her undersamlinger er komplette 
fra Kina, som I dag selv laver, og sendt herop og få det samlet i Slovakiet, hvor I så selv får det 
samlet i Danmark eller et eller andet, prøv hør det er der ikke nogen grund til, vi ved at andre med 
held har gjort det og det ud fra vores erfaringer, det synes jeg er mere interessant end at snakke om 
benchmark typisk, men der er også andre, noget omkring, hvor stor organisationen skal være det 
kan typiske være et rigtig godt sanity tjek på det, er de ikke lidt mange der? Eller bruger de ikke lidt 
mange penge på IT.  Eller hvorfor det og hvorfor det? Og hvad med R&D, igen lad os lige få 
tjekket hvad gennemsnittet er på industri på tværs af de forskellige områder. Det kan give et rigtigt

teaser, så der er noget med indikativ bud, eller så får man en IM, hvis du underskriver en eller

proces, at vi kigger ind i det, hvor vi skal ind at præsentere et eller andet her. Og så vil vi typisk 
starte med en management præsentation, så kan man sige, hvordan ser processen ud inde i, kort 
fortalt du har ikke tid til at lave en projektplan fordi et skal gå så stærkt, det er jo ikke sådan, at du 
går ind og siger godt guys vi skal lige have en projektplan, der er en milepæl her, vi skal være 
færdig med det her og her, vi prøver en gang imellem, men vi sidder altid oppe og knokler derud af. 
Det der kendetegner de her projekter er at informationsniveauet stiger og stiger men du skal hele 
tiden levere et eller andet output, men du ved først det du rigtig ved til sidst, når du skal sidde og

udfordringen er typisk, at lige meget hvad du gør så den første uge træder du vande, fordi du bliver 
klogere og klogere, du er i gang med at lave noget, og så stiger trykket bare mens du producerer i 
virkeligheden, så kan man sige, okay, er der nogle ting derunder? Jamen selvfølgelig. Vi starter jo 
med en hypoteseafdækning sammen med køber, det er typisk noget med at ind og mødes med dem, 
snakke det igennem og sige, hvad tænker de omkring deres syn på hvad der kan betyder noget 
omkring værdiansættelse, samtidig kommer de med sådan et præliminært scope af en art, lidt 
afhængigt af hvordan det foregår, så vil man gå til management præsentation på baggrund af det, så 
har du MP herinde og så har du færdig scope aftale med dem. Et eller andet sted herinde, der laver 
du en færdig aftale med dem om, hvordan projektet fra vores side skal se ud, hvor mange mand der 
skal på i hvor lang tid, det kommer lidt an på, der er ikke nogen fast form her, det er jo noget med at 
løse det, mens man arbejder med det, men på et eller andet tidspunkt her, der har vi en kontrakt 
omkring, hvordan arbejdet skal se ud, og vi har management præsentationen. Scopet består af nogle 
hypoteser omkring, hvordan vi tror situationen ser ud. Enten hypotesedrevet, et hypotesetræ 
omkring vi har de her hypoteser, eller et issue træ, vi har de her issues vi skal have adresseret. Vi 
arbejder mere med issues når det er operationens, og mere med hypoteser når det er kommercielt, 
det er min erfaring, men jeg ved ikke, om det bare er historik. Så har vi det her issuetræ, som giver 
indholdsfortegnelsen på vores arbejde, og hvad vi skal afdække. På baggrund af den, vil vi typisk 
prøver at planlægge de her tre uger omkring, hvad er det for nogle ting vi skal prøve at have klar til 
hvornår. Det er jo det vi prøver, og så finder vi hurtigt ud af, at vi ikke har den information vi skal 
bruge, fra vi requeste i datarummet, der går fem dage inden vi får svar, så bliver du nød til at lave 
noget andet i mens, og arbejde total parallelt og få lavet så meget arbejde som muligt, generiske 
slides du ved du skal bruge osv. osv. lige pludselig så skal du lige to dage til Slovakiet og en tur til 
Kina, fordi du skal ud at besøge fabrikken, afsted tilbage igen og arbejde videre. Men hen over 
denne her periode så begynder de her underpunkter at blive adresseret og du begynder at kunne tage 
konklusioner. Et eller andet tidspunkt her, 2/3 dele henne måske, så vil du til dem, det her har vi 
afklaret, det her har vi afklaret, vi arbejder videre med resten af de her underissues. Så vil vi så i 
processen derhenne arbejde videre, men som sagt, det er jo ikke sådan, at en halvdel er ordnet på en 
halv del af tiden, det er jo typisk sådan at 1/3 er ordnet når 2/3 af tiden er gået og resten på den 
sidste 1/3 af tiden, fordi du skal sætte dig ind i så mange ting, og du ved først hvordan det ser ud de 
sidste tre dage, det er der hvor du skaber den største værdi, for der har du fuldstændig styr på 
virksomheden, du ved hvem der laver hvad, og du drager alle de rigtig konklusioner, du har bare 
ikke tid til at producere alle slidsne, de skal helst være færdig før og så kan du rette i 
konklusionerne i virkeligheden. Så det er typisk, hvordan de tre uger ser ud i en større ramme.

C: Er der nogle ting som er rigtig rigtig vigtig at få gjort tidligt for at sikre, at man når i mål på en

M: Hmm hmm man kan sige, jo mere tid du bruger på scope i starten og skriver præcis, hvad du

arbejder for er ikke superskarpe på, hvad vi mener, når vi skriver en hypotese, så det er mere 
internt, hvad er det præcist vi mener, når vi skriver det her at vi er sådan ret skarpe på, hvad er det 
indholdsfortegnelsen skal være, og det synes jeg også vi gør ret meget, vi har jo et bruttoslides vi 
normalt sammensætter en pakke ud af, der i virkeligheden er standard, og så tilpasser vi og bruger

god ide, men jeg vil sige, det er jo scope-øvelsen, men jeg synes mere, det er nogle andre ting det 
handler om, så rent praktiske ting, det handler om at finde de rigtige folk, til den rigtige tid og have 
dem til rådighed fra starten af, og det er ikke noget med, at man skal tre dage afsted på et eller andet 
internt, det skal bare være, du ved alle skal være til rådighed  fuld tid i den periode, og så skal det 
nok gå, det er sådan det vigtigste.  
 
C: Der fx noget med alignment i forhold til kapitalfonden eller i forhold til køber, er der ligesom

M: Vi snakker bare meget sammen, og et relativt tæt forhold, men jeg tror som jeg sagde, de der 
præliminære scope, hvor vi ligesom kommer med hver vores udlægning af casen, hvad vi tror der er 
vigtigt og blive enige om det, hvor vi har normalt nogle punkter de ikke har tænkt over, og de har 
rent faktisk også nogle punkter, som vi ikke har tænkt over rent evaluerings øjemed, eller hvad 
deres formål med købet er, og så ligesom holde hinanden oppe på det. Normalt har vi et kald hvert 
fald en gang om ugen os som rådgiver, hvor vi også koordinerer med de andre rådgiver, hvad er det 
vi kigger på osv osv.  Det er for det meste retningen, det synes jeg fungerer godt. 
 
C: Hvordan bliver den viden man opsamler i ODD’en, i tilfælde af køb, hvordan den bliver trukket 
videre over til post-acquisition? 
 
M: Min erfaringer er normalt, at efter vi har lavet en udgave af dokumentet, som er anonymiseret i 
forhold til at target selv skal kunne læse den, så får de faktiske den udleveret, hvad vores rådgivning 
er. Helt afhængig af virksomheden, så vil de tage det som en gave eller som noget de slet ikke kan 
forholde sig til, og man kan sige, der kan de blive inspireret til at gøre de her ting anderledes, og 
sige jamen prøv og hør det her er en skide god ide, kan vi ikke lige snakke med dem, der har lavet 
det og kom over og fortælle. Det har vi oplevet. Men vi har også oplevet, at den bare er blevet smidt 
ud, for det er sådan noget vi ikke bruger i virksomheden, det er også okay. Så har vi også været ud 
for at realisere nogle af de ting vi har fundet ud af, det er jo ikke usædvanligt, som sådan, man kan 
sige, vi arbejder jo med mange af de her fonde med at lave nogle koncepter, for hvordan de adresser 
og realiserer og udvælger og prioriterer mange af de temaer de virksomheder de køber. Der har vi jo 
lavet en standard, et stort framework, for én dansk kapitalfond, og vi har også et standard format, ja 
faktisk to, men det ene er transmissionsformat og det andet er hvad er de vigtigste values leavers er 
i forhold til den her virksomhed. For her virksomhed, så er det de her vi skal prioritere, og derfor 
går vi ud og vælger dem ud og går i gang med dem i virkeligheden. Ikke nødvendigvis med os som 
drivende faktor mere som faciliterende for at finde ud af om de så har brug for hjælp til at få det 
gjort bagefter, men normalt er det mere i forhold til faciliterende i forhold til at udvælge hvilke ting 
==PAGE:151==
 
 
 
Master Thesis: Operational Due Diligence Framework

man skal gå i gang med først og lave en overordnet plan. Det er jo både det kommercielle og det 
operationelle  
 
C: Er der noget i forhold til framework og proces du tænker der kunne gøre det nemmere for dig at 
udføre en ODD.  
 
M: Ja ja, der jo selvfølgelig masser af ting. Det er jo typisk noget med at sige, det er jo på sælgers 
præmisser, det er sælger der laver en tidsplan, som er stram, begrænset, det her må I få  at vide det 
er med lukkede bøger, men vi åbner nogle af dem her og her. Vi stiller og selv til rådighed i det her 
format, problemet er bare, at det gør de også, men der er seks om buddet, så det bliver meget lidt, så 
selv om man har adgang til meget information, så det der med at komme helt tæt på, er ikke altid 
let. Så bare det, jeg ved ikke om man kan gøre noget ved det, men det er jo et resultat af at det er 
med de fortrolighedsforhold, der nu en gang er gældende. Det gør det bare svært at være en del af 
den proces, fordi man ligesom skal komme med et bud og har ikke adgang til særlig meget 
information. En anden ting er også hele tidsrammen og aspektet, hvis man bare kunne blive advaret 
et par uger inden, så man kan planlægge sin tid og arbejdet i stedet for, NU er det alvor, det der med 
at PE fonden, i højere grad tænker de rigtig rådgivning ind i tide. Det gør de nogle gange og de gør 
det når vi kommer med casen og promoverer den, og siger se den her, den er rigtig god. Det er 
noget vi kender, vi meddeler i god tid. Sidder med en nu hvor jeg har seks uger, det har jeg ikke 
oplevet før, men det er jo fordi, vi er ude i så god tid, jo mere af det fra vores side, vil gøre arbejdet 
meget bedre, fordi jeg ved godt vi er meget intelligente mennesker, men vi kan ikke smide alt og gå 
i gang med at lave en DD med ordentlig kvalitet bare på baggrund af vores erfaring, fordi det er 
virkeligheden forskelligt, vi skal have de rigtig punkter og det rigtige materiale og vi skal forberede 
os på det og vi skal finde de rigtige folk, så hvis man kunne være ude i bedre tid, så tror jeg også vi 
kunne levere et bedre stykke arbejde.
